Supplement to the Shanghai Edition of the Shen Bao

Speeches

American Diplomat Fires Blanks 221

— Xing An

Pittman, Chairman of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee of the United States, who referred to Japan as an "international robber" last December, recently delivered an important speech in the Senate, fiercely criticizing Japan's China policy. He stated that Japan is now determined to destroy the Nine-Power Treaty, close the door to China, and that the United States should expand its naval and air forces to maintain the dignity of peace treaties.

Pittman's speech is a response to Japan's unlimited aggression against China. The current Far East issue has once again become a problem of conflict between the Open Door Policy and the East Asia hegemony. Japan wants to block China's door, while Britain and the United States insist on equal sharing of interests in China. The Nine-Power Treaty, signed in 1922 by Britain, the United States, Japan, France, Italy, Belgium, the Netherlands, Portugal, and China, stipulated respect for China's sovereignty, independence, and territorial integrity, and adherence to the principle of equal opportunity for the commercial interests of all countries. However, this treaty has been destroyed by Japan since the September 18th Incident, so Britain and the United States cannot sit idly by, and conflicts have repeatedly occurred with Japan. Pittman's attack on Japan is also due to this.

However, Pittman's stern words, although not without benefit to the critical Far East situation, are ultimately just empty words. Japan's destruction of the Nine-Power Treaty is already very obvious. Despite the statement by the Japanese Foreign Ministry authorities that "Japan's policy towards East Asia aims to establish peace and is by no means to break the Open Door Policy or to monopolize East Asia by force," and the response from Japanese newspapers that "Japan has never infringed upon China's sovereignty, nor does it have any intention of infringing upon it in the future," the occupation of territories, the plunder of the twenty-two counties in eastern Hebei, and the control of several provinces in North China—what is this if not East Asia? What is this if not infringement of sovereignty? This kind of ostrich-like sophistry only further exposes its wildness. However, the signatory countries of the Nine-Power Treaty can only express their protest with a few empty words regarding Japan's actions, and dare not take effective measures to stop it. This has allowed the unbridled ambition of the ambitious to disrupt peace in East Asia. Therefore, although the destroyer of the Nine-Power Treaty is Japan's military force, the failure of the relevant countries to fulfill the obligations stipulated in the treaty also contributes to this.

In fact, we are not saying this in the hope that various countries will exert effort for China in order to fight for their own interests. We are only pointing out the failure of various countries to comply with the obligations of the treaty. In order to maintain the survival of our country, we have our own responsibilities to fulfill. Pittman's speech, no matter how sternly spoken, is unlikely to awaken Japan from its delusions. British official circles observe most clearly, saying that Pittman's words "only express anti-Japanese sentiments, and it cannot be concluded that the United States will take strong action to stop Japan's outward expansion, which is out of line." Even Britain admits that "Britain itself has not found a way to resist Japan." Therefore, in order to seek China's sovereignty, independence, and territorial integrity, it still depends on the efforts of the Chinese people themselves.

Spring Book 222

— Hua Zhi

It is already spring. The city is sensitive; perhaps one can see fashionable ladies wearing new spring clothes on the wide sidewalks. But, released from that severely cold small town, I still have lingering fears of the harsh weather. Since I came to this small town, there has been little communication. Are you wondering if I don't even have the time to write a letter? This is what the severe winter has given me. I had not even passed the fifteenth of December when I arrived in this town. Collecting accounts in the countryside is the easiest thing; they have already prepared the funds and are waiting for your bill to arrive. At the slowest, it wouldn't take more than a week. But when I had collected all the accounts and was preparing to leave, winter bared its fangs and exercised its authority: it was a heavy snowstorm. When you walk on the field bank and look back at the places you have walked, you can no longer find any trace. So, like a vagrant, I was confined to a small inn all day. The inn was so small, separated by the cheapest wooden boards, as if it were a birdcage. After the Dali steamer stopped running, there was no way to leave. It was difficult to find a newspaper, let alone buy some books to pass the time. I had no way to pass these days when I was so eager to return home. Lying in bed, the long sighs of the travelers in the next room made me think of my home even more—it was the end of December, and a family is not as easy to spend the New Year as a bachelor! My white-haired old mother, my young wife, my young children, they are all leaning on the door, waiting for my return. Perhaps they will go to the dock to welcome me when the ship arrives. How disappointed they must be!

The innkeeper is also a foreigner. He welcomes me, the customer who comes every year; we are very familiar. When he is free, he brings his water pipe to my room to chat. He can light one paper match after another and talk to you from afternoon to dusk. However, he doesn't tell jokes; he is used to saying things that make people angry. I hate him very much, but I have no reason to refuse him from coming to my room. I am so conflicted. I would prefer him to report to me that a steamer will depart tomorrow, so that even if he talks to me until dawn, I can excitedly carry my luggage and rush to the steamer dock, treading on the muddy snow, not looking like someone who hasn't slept all night. One evening, it was the day we sent off the Kitchen God in my hometown. At dinnertime, he still hadn't thought of leaving my room. I was about to use this as an excuse to send him away when the waiter brought a plate of fairly rich dishes to my room. The boss put down his water pipe, placed the plates of food in the center of the table, and said to me in that weak voice, "My wife specially made a few dishes, how about we drink a few cups of wine?" He was so hesitant, afraid that I would suddenly refuse him. But I thanked him very much. How much did every cell in my body need to be excited? I thanked him for doing something I couldn't think of—drinking a few cups of wine, even though my alcohol tolerance is very small. That day, of course, I was drunk. That day must have been the most enjoyable!

Here, I also want to tell you something. For so many days, like a defeated rooster, I was locked in a small room. Every day I hoped that the night would come early. It would be a pleasure to have a sound sleep! But the patrol team in this small town is very excellent. Four people in a group, three people in a team, holding a triangular flag with a red seal, before it gets dark, they come to inspect the travelers. The way they look, I simply can't think of an appropriate metaphor for a while. The one in the lead holds a traveler's circulation book, asking what is your last name, what is your name, where do you come from, where are you going, what are you doing. Sometimes they even inspect your luggage for no reason. Every day from four or five in the afternoon until dawn, you have to be interrogated more than ten times, and there is simply no time to sleep peacefully. Later, I opened the door to sleep. When they came in, I didn't wait for their interrogation and recited a clean record like memorizing a book. So I am even more grateful to my innkeeper. That day I was drunk, and I don't know how those things were inspected.

But none of those things are good people. During the day, I often see them in the empty rooms of the inn, forcing the waiter to call for flower girls, venting their bestial desires, and slipping away without spending a penny. At night, they put on a serious face under the triangular flag. It is said that they were specially transferred from the county town for winter defense. Think about it, how many people will be oppressed and insulted by them this winter?

There are so many things in this small town that make people unable to stand it. I escaped like a pardoned prisoner. I'll talk to you in detail when I have the opportunity.

Page 20

Grandpa's Story 223

— Ai Mei

In February, a terrifying whirlwind swept in from Tiger Head Mountain, three hundred miles away, dissipating the deathly air in the town and scattering all the worries in people's hearts! Grandpa usually got up early, and he was even more worried these years. Although he was an old man, he was as strong and robust as he was in his youth. It was still only dimly lit, there was no sun, and there was not a trace of cloudy rain. It was gray and gloomy, and the corners of the eaves were quietly blowing wind. Everyone was still asleep, but Grandpa's familiar cough sounded stuffy from the front wing room, and then the sound of getting up and opening the door was heard.

After clearing his throat for a while, he sat on a homemade short stool, his spirit very excited, holding his old, balding pipe in his mouth, smoking leisurely, but in his heart he was planning: labor, market prices, plowing cattle, and the food and use of a family of more than a dozen people..., so he sighed. From the age of six, he followed his father to collect pig and dog manure everywhere, until the age of fifty-five now, he had never felt himself old. He was strong and capable, using means like an old fox to deal with worldly affairs, but now, he could only sigh...

Like Grandpa, Uncle Qiaojiao, an old elder in the village, was also worried. He couldn't stand the wild, short-haired, bare-chested, civilized female students in the town. He couldn't stand the price of twelve yuan for a stone of rice. He couldn't stand the young people who liked to eat, were lazy, liked to do good things, and made trouble. In short, he couldn't stand everything in the current world, so he also felt old.

These two old elders had been friends for decades. Whenever there was something they couldn't figure out, Grandpa would often go to his house, and Uncle Qiaojiao would receive him. The two old men would laugh happily, as if they had suddenly become young again. And Uncle Qiaojiao would also often come to visit for ant-like trivial matters.

A few years ago, Grandpa wanted to save some money to buy a plowing cow, but he didn't have any money, so he went to Uncle Qiaojiao's house with a cane, just as Uncle Qiaojiao was also coming over because he wanted to import a coffin for himself. The two old men met on the road, so they went together to sit under the cypress tree on the ridge of the field. Grandpa lamented the plight of a farmer without plowing cattle, and Uncle Qiaojiao explained his decades of labor and toil like a horse. Could it be that he didn't even have a decent coffin? No! He had to save some money himself. Seeing that his unfilial son would never plan for him again, because the fifth grandson was about to be born. They sighed, reporting their plans to each other, from their daily salt, soy sauce, vinegar, all the way to how to save a few tubes of dry tobacco. Finally, they went home with their canes.

After dinner, Grandpa announced his new policy for managing the family. He hadn't been to the fields for several years. Now he also shouldered the hoe and went to the fields with his sons, so that he could plant more vegetables in the wheat field to sell in the town. Back home, he also walked around with a cane, scolding, to see who had wasted a match, to see who had wasted the kerosene in the oil lamp. So he turned red in the face, tapped his cane, and loudly said that food was difficult and that saving was important. In this way, he also placed a small wooden cabinet on his bedside, dug a small hole on it, locked the cabinet door, and told everyone in the family that they must save food and automatically donate copper coins. In this way, Grandpa quickly turned the copper coins into dimes, and then exchanged the dimes into bright silver dollars, wrapped them in paper, firmly placed them in his waistband, and went to town with Uncle Qiaojiao. There was a farmer's bank run by the government in the town, which was considered to have good credit within a hundred and fifty miles. Grandpa completed the transaction at the bank, deposited the money, carefully put the deposit book in his waistband, and returned home satisfied. That night, Grandpa first drank white wine, trembling with excitement, and told of a terrible and prosperous fortune that was about to come to our family, because we would soon have a fat plowing cow.

"At that time," Grandpa said emotionally, "you can proudly wave your whips, driving the village to the hillside. Everyone must be attracted out of the house by this unusual plowing cow, looking with surprised eyes, enviously asking: Whose is this decent plowing cow? And you, children, must loudly, without fear, answer: Our grandfather saved money to buy it! Then the viewers will carefully touch the cow's body, sighing, spreading the news throughout the town, even the district chief will hear about it..." Grandpa was excited and shed tears.

The next day, we were allowed to have a meat meal. But Grandpa's happy days didn't last long, and they were shattered! A terrifying whirlwind swept across the town, and it was rumored in the village that the farmer's bank was about to close. Uncle Qiaojiao's face turned green, panting, his cane tapping sharply on the stone threshold, bringing this ominous news. Grandpa was startled, dragged out the cane from the bedside, carefully opened the lock on the small wooden cabinet, took out the deposit book from the bank, and ran towards the town with Uncle Qiaojiao in large strides. The family was as silent as death, and black clouds covered all the small gaps. A terrible threat was slowly growing and swelling.

In the afternoon, Grandpa came back with his cane, disheartened, hopeless, without saying a word, sitting on a low wooden stool, staring blankly in a daze. After thinking for a while, he sighed sadly, tremblingly ran into the room, took out the wooden cabinet containing the copper coins, and smashed it hard against the courtyard. The small wooden cabinet hit the stone with a loud bang and shattered, copper coins scattered all over the ground, but Grandpa stood there blankly, clenching his hands, biting his teeth. When everyone looked at him, those two old eyes had already dripped a few lines of tears.

Lies 224

— (Fool)

Yoshizawa returned to his country the other day and talked about the purpose of diplomacy towards China, which lies in the establishment of the "Three Principles." Now, we should start from the most important Japan-Manchukuo-China cooperation of the "Three Principles" to promote it. Tan Lao San said that our country was originally the Three Principles of the People, Five Races United in Harmony, but now it has become the Three Principles and Six Races United in Harmony, which is truly something that one could never have imagined.

Jin Tongyi, the former section chief of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, was detained by the court for falling in love with Liu Zhaofen, a female student from Soochow University, and plotting to harm his wife, Li. This matter caused a sensation in Nanjing last year. Now, Li has filed a lawsuit with the Shanghai Second Special Zone Court, requesting to divorce Jin. Tan Lao San said that our people are originally suitable for polygamy, but now the law stipulates a one-husband-one-wife system, no wonder there are so many divorce cases.

In Zhai County (Continued) 225

— Hua

We finally settled down in a small shop. At that time, the western sky was weaving colorful brocade clouds, and the slick faces of every pedestrian on the street reflected that beautiful red light. My companion was washing his face, and said jokingly:

"If you boil this basin of washing water, you can get half a catty of salt."

This small shop has a small courtyard. Several guests are drinking large cups of tea there. We are all from the same hometown, and we are all going to Annam.

Since we are new guests, everyone is vying to ask about Tangshan, long and short. The first thing they ask about is Japan. An old foreigner asked me in his half-salty, half-sweet Chaozhou dialect;

"You are a scholar, do you think China will prosper or not? Do we have to wait for the true emperor to come out?"

"I say," another person interjected, he is a medicinal material merchant who often travels between Saigon and Shantou, "If China continues like this, it will definitely not prosper. Think about it, the situation is getting worse every year, and we don't have airplanes or warships, and..."

"Everything is destiny," my friend snatched and said, "If you don't believe it, Yue Fei wanted to save the Great Song Dynasty, but Qin Hui came along. The Great Song Dynasty was supposed to perish, isn't that destiny? Nothing is useful, nothing is useful!"

"If you say that, then we are destined to die. I don't believe it. We are China, the world's largest country in ancient and modern times. Everything you say is unfounded, I don't believe it. Do you agree, sir?" the old man said.

He looked at me. I was a little dazed and didn't know how to answer. They have been away from their hometown for too long, and years of life have given them nothing but pain and no spiritual food. Do you want to laugh at their ignorance? But they all have a passionate heart.

The sky is slowly darkening. A trace of cool breeze floats over the small courtyard from time to time. The stars in the southern country seem particularly bright, shining brightly, embedded in the azure sky. All kinds of strange insect sounds float around, and there also seems to be a hissing sound of snakes.

When I turned back from outside, my friend who believed in fate was already sound asleep, snoring loudly. In the small courtyard, the old fellow was still deeply absorbed in sucking on a long pipe. The other two people, one seemed to be dozing off, but one wanted to talk about the market conditions for batch water. One asked, and the other waited a long time before answering a sentence. Soon, both of them were sound asleep.

I was dozing off when suddenly someone tapped me on the shoulder. I woke up immediately. Under the faint moonlight, I saw that the old man was on my right. His expression was sincere and still serious.

"Our China should be stronger, but, sir, tell me, can we become strong?"

I didn't answer, staring blankly at the old man.

. His eyes were like they were on fire.

Ballad 229

Xu Wenbi's Opening

City Tone (1340) 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM

Opening: "Dream of the Red Chamber Tune" (Part 1)

In the first month, plum blossoms bloom in scattered beauty. With pepper flowers, we offer praises to wish for a happy new year. Whose residence can rival the splendor of the Rong Mansion as the feast is laid out? The silver candle casts a cold light on the painted screen. Lantern Festival night. Admiring lanterns and blossoms. All under heaven rejoice together in peace and prosperity. Cleverly, Mandarin Duck crafts ivory tablet games. Rousing poets to speak of it to this day. Intoxicated by the east wind, February lengthens. Within the Welcome Spring Pavilion, a hundred flowers bloom. The fair maiden idly plants grass in the deep courtyard. Applying new reds to Shanghai crabapple blossoms. Head full of verdure. Hands full of fragrance. The spirit platform's springtime color is unparalleled. Myriad purples and reds are worthy of entering paintings. Poets lay down their pens, struggling to compose commentary. In the third month of Wuling, the little peach blossoms blush red. Where is Tan Chun fishing for duckweed? The beautiful sun is warm, the fragrant grass green. Supporting me with a cane, I cross the bridge to the east. Frightened swallows dart. Butterflies accompany bees. The jade branches intertwined, their shadows exquisite. The fragrance of flowers assaults, knowing the painting's warmth. The willow wind that brushes the face is not cold. As the moon sets on fading flowers, sorrowfully I lean on the railing. When will Xi Chun return? Fallen reds cover the ground, unswept by anyone. Willow catkins pave a white felt mat on the three paths. The wind blows gently. The sun is radiant. Long and slow, as the years drag on, the partridge sings to heaven. Sitting alone, embracing the qin, I sing a tune. Stealing half a day of leisure from this floating life. In the fifth month, pomegranate flowers bloom, scattering lingering sunset hues. Fengjie's arrival brings auspicious omens, her colorful attire concealing her. Her innate beauty is unmatched. The plums left sour, spurting saliva from the teeth. Talent surpasses all. Appearance is exceptional. A single branch of spring occupies a full ten points of value. Jade bracelets ring on her pale wrists. Banana leaves record events on the gauze window. In the listless sixth month, too lazy to paint eyebrows. An ice-silk fan is carried in hand to brush the face. Dense shade, cicadas chirp among silk trees. The mountain colors are hazy, the rain is also extraordinary. Freshly bathed. The evening breeze is faint. Where the pearl curtain is flung, the setting sun is to the west. Near the pond, Xiang Ling has let flowers bloom everywhere. A clear pool that can soak the poet's spleen.

Lu Qiuxia's Double Pearl Phoenix

Sino-Western (1040) 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM

Opening: "Dream of the Red Chamber Tune" (Part 2)

In the seventh month, the golden phoenix ascends the small building. Lightly furrowing her brows, Daiyu's jade face is filled with sorrow. Gazing afar, where is her hometown? White clouds and red leaves, both leisurely and far away. Xiaoxiang Pavilion. Shanghai, hidden and secretive. Wounds from spring's lament, sadly linked to the Cowherd. The purple oriole cries through the third watch of the moon. Going south and coming north, rest no more. Sweet osmanthus scents drift in the eighth month sky. Xiang Yun emerges from the eastern hills, carrying the moon. Next door, the sound of a pounding stone urges haste. The silver river is silent, turning the jade disc. The character "heaven" is pure. Dew is cold. On the hundred-foot tower, a person leans on the railing. In the courtyard, the autumn parasol trees are seen gradually falling. First hearing the migrating geese, there is no one who does not vie with the crabapple for clever smiles. Bamboo fences and thatched houses, content with their fate. Solitary and aloof, few kindred spirits. Sitting upright, idly consulting the Diamond Sutra. Moreover, Siqi is a companion. Not accepting even a speck of dust's invasion. In the tenth month of early winter, red blossoms are picked. Bao Qin's rich charm is unparalleled in the world. Her snow-like beauty complements and reflects against each other. Together with the plum blossoms, making a full ten points of spring. Poetry as companion. Brocade as heart. The person is on the first level of the Jade Terrace. The amber cup tilts, releasing rose dew. The Southern Mountain faces the door, turning distinctly. In the eleventh month, the cold wind enters the pines. Xiuyan is enveloped in the snowy wind. The beautiful woman warms herself in the chamber, roasting venison. The bamboo stove boils, the fire freshly red. Competing to chant verses. Rhyming words are skillful. The joy of tilting cups brings pleasure to the heart. Qingwen's beauty is like a myriad miles of rosy clouds. Only with plum blossoms is she different. In the twelfth month, snow presses a branch of flowers. Baochai cleverly leans towards the hair at the temples. The plum blossoms vie with the beauty for elegance and simplicity. In the snow, she plays with fragrance and dabbles in powder. Green vines are still. The jade face is lovely. Entering a charming state, truly worthy of praise. Moreover, there are the sparse shadows of Caiyun. Deeply submerged waters, shallowly enveloping sand. In the intercalary month, bored, I get drunk amidst the blossoms. Cherishing Baoyu's jade within my heart, encompassing the four seasons of spring. How many luxurious dandies are there? Only the sunflower inclines towards the sun. Thousand-day red. Evergreen. Gauze windows and cold bamboo form neighbors. The jade box has not been opened, the Wu Hook sword has not been drawn. Seeking a Peach Blossom Spring to escape the Qin Dynasty.

Movie News

Epic Film "Charlie Chan's Secret" 231

Premiering Today at the Grand Theatre

Charlie Chan detective cases have been continuously produced on the silver screen because he is a Chinese detective, so such films have particularly good box office revenue in the Chinese film market, and the male star Warner Oland, who plays Charlie Chan, has become famous as a result. Now, "Charlie Chan's Secret" is scheduled to premiere at the Grand Theatre today (Wednesday). The content is shrouded in mystery, full of dangerous situations, and becomes more interesting the more you watch. This is said to be Warner Oland's most proud and precious work, even more tense and exciting than all previous Charlie Chan detective cases.

Miscellaneous Notes on the Preview of "Spring Flower" 232

— Gao Mei

Late at night, the preview of "Spring Flower" at the Central Cinema for the first time.

Tan Ying wore black glasses and sat with Bu Gao in the back row. Wu Cun also wore black glasses and was talking to someone in the back. Li Pingqian also rushed over after finishing work on the set of "Peach and Plum's Anxious Beauty". Sun Min nodded to Pingqian in a very leisurely manner. Wang Jiting ran over to greet Tan Ying and Bu Gao. Many other leading actors did not come. Only Yan Yuexian also rushed over when the lights dimmed.

The intoxicating rhythm of a love song propelled the melody of the entire story. This sweet song formed a medium between Old Gao and Second Sister Yuexian. In this annoying song, Old Gao had no gold and no woman. In the middle of this sweet song's rhythm, it is unknown how many heavy changes and twists and turns were experienced. The final ending was that Second Sister Yuexian committed suicide for this song, and the man with the rough voice vowed never to sing this hateful song again.

Old Gao's solid acting goes without saying. Second Sister plays a singer who transitions from wild joy to sorrow with great emotion. Huang Naishuang and Xie Yunqing both put in a lot of effort. You Guangzhao and Zhu Qiuhen's performances are mostly humorous. Wu Cun's daughter, Little Pearl, is extremely cute.

There are extremely beautiful scenes and very skilled techniques. There are even more gimmicks, including a comedy inserted into a film set. The latest issue of Star Bi-Monthly says it is doing "self-satire", which is truly wonderful!

A Scene from "Iron-Blooded General"

Soon to Premiere at the Grand Theatre

Chronicle of the Preparations for the Public Performance of the Insect Voice Society 233

Among the many emerging small theater troupes in 1936, the Insect Voice Society can be considered one of the most well-established. Not long after their formation, they ambitiously wanted to launch a grand alliance of theater stages to hold a public performance. At the current stage of the rising national liberation struggle movement, how urgently needed is this! However, although many groups responded to this initiative, as a result of discussions, due to the difficulty in raising funds, it was ultimately put on hold for the time being. At the same time, they also deeply felt that not giving society a good impression and society's inability to provide assistance was inevitable. On the one hand, they were unwilling to disappoint the enthusiastic requests from the masses who held high hopes for them, and finally decided to hold a public performance on their own.

However, the encouragement from countless new messengers who love the art of drama who have joined in succession is also considerable.

They are very strict about the selection of plays, and have repeatedly changed them. Currently, the ones that have been decided on include Tian Han's new play "Bugle Call". There are two songs in the play. The effect of Qian Ying, a member of the society, singing the leading role of the eldest daughter is unknown. They are not confident and will wait for future social criticism.

Others include Yu Chu's "Doing Good and Giving Generously" and "Father, Son, and Brothers", which will soon be able to meet with people from all walks of life.

Silver Pen News 234

— Zhi Er

At the "Six Arts" literary salon tea party, attendees included "well-known figures in the literary world, including the journal's editors, modernist masters" Mu Shiying, Liu Na'ou, Ye Lingfeng, who "never lets go of his book", and Gao Ming, "the angry-faced teacher Gao", among others. The publisher and editor, Yao Sufeng, was conspicuously absent. The reason is unknown.

Anna May Wong has been more in the spotlight these days than Hu Die. It is said that Hu Die was expelled from Fujian, while Anna May Wong has been busy attending banquets these days. In addition to banquets hosted by Mayor Wu and others, yesterday (17th), Lu Shouli of the International Hotel also "prepared tea and refreshments" on the 14th floor of the hotel's ballroom.

Humor master Lin Yutang attended the banquet for Anna May Wong at the International Hotel. Some say: Lin Yutang should have gone because Anna May Wong once greatly praised our Master Lin when talking to guests, wasn't it? Courtesy demands reciprocity. Master Lin, the founder of "The Analects", had an inescapable duty to go.

"Parents and Children of Culture" is said to be screened at the Jin Cheng Cinema this Friday. As it concerns the life of "Culture", it cannot but be paid attention to.

The Lianhua Pictorial will publish a special memorial issue for the first anniversary of Ms. Ruan Lingyu's death. Contributions from all walks of life are welcome. Works commemorating Ms. Ruan should be sent to Lianhua Pictorial, No. 3, Triangle Street, Xujiahui, Shanghai, before February 25.
